mysql> # and where is replaced with on keyword

mysql> # limitation of using ..................................
mysql> # the coloumn name must be same in both or in many tables then and then only using keyword works
mysql> #.................................. Natural join ..................................
mysql> # it will joins the coloumn which are identical in the both tables
mysql> desc dept;
+-----------+-------------+------+-----+---------+-------+
| Field     | Type        | Null | Key | Default | Extra |
+-----------+-------------+------+-----+---------+-------+
| DEPTNO    | int         | NO   | PRI | NULL    |       |
| DNAME     | varchar(12) | YES  |     | NULL    |       |

mysql> #.................................. Simple Join ..................................
mysql> #......................................................................................................
mysql> # simple join is same as natural join
mysql> # the only change is we have to give the condition
mysql> # by using the keywords -- 'using' and 'on'
mysql> # the limitation of 'using' keyword is applicable in simple join also
mysql> # i.e. the coloumn names must be same in both the tables
mysql> select * from emp simple join dept using(deptno);

ERROR 1064 (42000): You have an error in your SQL syntax; check the manual that corresponds to your MySQL server version for the right syntax to use near '@a,@b from emp' at line 1
mysql> select max(sal),min(sal) into @a,@b from emp;
Query OK, 1 row affected (0.01 sec)

mysql> # it stores the value of Minimum salary and maximum salary into a variable 'a' and 'b'
mysql> select @a;
+------+
| @a   |
+------+
| 5000 |
+------+
1 row in set (0.00 sec)

mysql> select @b;

| @b   |
+------+
|  800 |
+------+
1 row in set (0.00 sec)
